[Brahman.тАФsaptatriс╣Е┼Ыat. br─Бhm─Бudaniham. tr─Бiс╣гс╣нubham: 1. anuс╣гс╣нubgarbh─Б bhurik pan╠Дkti; 2. bс╣Ыhat─лgarbh─Б vir─Бj; 3. 4-p. ┼Ы─Бkvaragarbh─Б jagat─л; 4. bhurij; 5. brhat─лgarbh─Б vir─Бj; 6. uс╣гс╣Зih; 8. vir─Бdg─Бyatr─л; 6. ┼Ы─Бkvar─Бtij─Бgaiagarbh─Б jagat─л; 10. vir─Бс╣н purotijagat─л vir─Бс╕Нjagat─л; 11. jagat─л; 15, 16. bhurij; 17. vir─Бс╕Н jagat─л; 18. atij─Бgatagarbh─Б par─Бtij─Бgat─Б vir─Бс╕Н atijagat─л; 20. atij─Бgatagarbh─Б para┼Ы─Бkvar─Б 4-p. bhurig jagat─л; 21, 24-26, 29. vir─Бс╕Нjagat─л (29. bhurij); 27. atij─Бgatagarbh─Б jagat─л; 3i. bhurij; 35. 4-p. kakummaty uс╣гс╣Зih; 36. purovir─Бс╕Н vy─Бghr─Бdiс╣гv avagantavy─Б*; 37. vir─Бс╕Н jagat─л.]

Comment

тМКVerse 35 is prose.тМЛ Found also in P─Бipp. xvi. (in the verse-order 1-10, 12, 11, 13-18, 22, 19, 20, 21, 23-37). Nearly every verse of the hymn is quoted in K─Бu┼Ы. 60-63 and 65 in connection with the description of the sava offerings; тМКsee Bloomfield, page 610 and the following for details so far as they are helpfulтМЛ. тМКCitations in other parts of K─Бu┼Ы. are noted under the verses. The hymn is not noticed by V─Бit.: see page 610.тМЛ *тМКThis curious addition to the Anukr., vy─Бghr─Бdiс╣гv avagantavy─Б, recurs in the Anukr’s treatment of xiv. 1. 60 and of the c of xv. 5. 1-7. See note to xv. 5. 7.тМЛ

Whitney
Translation
  1. O Agni, be thou born; Aditi here, suppliant, cooks a
    brahm├бn-rice-dish, desiring sons; the seven seers, being-makersтАФlet
    them churn thee here together with progeny.
Notes

Aditi’s cooking of a rice-dish in order to obtain progeny is repeatedly
referred to in the Br─Бhmaс╣ЗasтАФprobably by way of echo of this verse:
compare TS. vi. 5. 6┬╣; TB. i. 1. 9┬╣; K. vii. 15; MS. i. 6. 12; тМКii. 1.
12 and referencesтМЛ; тМКalso AV. vi. 81. 3тМЛ; the comm. quotes the TS.
passage in his explanation of the verse. He defines a brahm─Бudana as
brahmaс╣Зe jagatsraс╣гс╣нre sv─Бh─Бkareс╣Зa deya odanaс╕е, and then adds: yad v─Б
brahm─Бudanasav─Бkhye тАШsmin karmaс╣Зi br─Бhmaс╣З─Бn─Бm bhojan─Бya bh─Бgatvena
kalpita odano brahm─Бudanaс╕е.

Griffith

Agni, spring forth! Here Aditi, afflicted, cooks a Brahmaudana, yearning for children. Let the Seven Rishis, World-creators, rub thee into existence here with gift of offspring.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Make ye smoke, O ye bulls, companions, ye that are aided by the
    unhateful (?), unto speech; this Agni [is] fight-overpowering, having
    good heroes, by whom the gods overpowered the barbarians.

Griffith

Raise, as I bid, the smoke, my strong companions, lovers of free- dom from deceit and malice! Victor in fight heroic, here is Agni by whom the Gods subdued the hostile demons.

  1. O Agni, thou hast been born unto great heroism, unto the cooking of
    the brahm├бn-rice-dish, O J─Бtavedas; the seven seers,

Griffith

Thou, Agni, wart produced for mighty valour, to cook Brahmau- dana, O Jatavedas. Seven Rishis, makers of the world, begat thee, Grant to this woman wealth with store of heroes.

Translation
  1. Kindled, O Agni, be thou kindled with kindling (sam├нdh); mayest
    thou bring hither, knowing, the worshipful gods; for them cooking

Griffith

Your portion from of old is triply parted, portion of Gods, of Fathers, and of mortals. Know, all, your shares. I deal them out among you. The portion of the Gods shall save this woman.

режрем рдЕрдЧреНрдиреЗ рд╕рд╣рд╕реНрд╡рд╛рдирднрд┐рднреВрд░рднреАрджрд╕рд┐ ...{Loading}...
Whitney
Translation
  1. O Agni, powerful, overcoming, thou overcomest; put down (ni-ubj)
    [our] hating rivals; let this measure (m─Б╠Бtr─Б), being measured, and
    measured, make [thy] fellows tribute-bringers to thee.
Notes

The comm. does not try to give ny ubja a more distinctive meaning than
adhomukh─Бn p─Бtaya; the obscure m─Б╠Бtr─Б he simply glosses by nirm─Бtr─Б
тМКas instrumental sing, masc. (supplying iyaс╣Б ┼Ы─Бl─Б as subject); but the
three translators take it as nom.тМЛ.

Griffith

Strong art thou, Agni, conquering, all-surpassing. Crush down our foemen, ruin those who hate us. So let this measure, measured, being measured, make all our kin thy tributary vassals.

Whitney
Translation
  1. In company with thy fellows, be thou united with milk; urge her up
    unto great heroism; ascend aloft to the summit (viс╣гс╣н├бp) of the
    firmament (n─Б╠Бka), which they call by the name heavenly world.
Notes

Addressed, according to the comm., to the sacrificer; the K─Бu┼Ы. (61. 20)
makes it accompany the pouring of rice into the mortar. The comm.
explains ud ubja as ud gamaya unnata┼Ыirask─Бс╣Б kuru. Ppp. reads
suj─Бt─Бiс╣г in a, and viс╣гс╣нapas in c.

Griffith

Increase with kinsmen and with all abundance: to mighty strength and power lift up this woman. Erect, rise upward to the sky’s high station, rise to the lofty world which men call Svarga.

режрео рдЗрдпрдВ рдорд╣реА ...{Loading}...
Whitney
Translation
  1. Let this great one (mah─л╠Б) accept the hide, the divine earth, with
    favoring mind; then may we go to the world of the well-done.
Notes

This accompanies, as is plain, the spreading-out of the ox-hide upon the
ground (so K─Бu┼Ы. 60. 30). Ppp. reads in b pс╣Ыthivy─Бi, and, at the
end, sukс╣Ыt─Бm u lokam. The last p─Бda is the same with vi. 121. 1 d;
vii. 83. 4 d.

Griffith

May this great Earth receive the skin, this Goddess Prithivi, showing us her love and favour. Then may we go unto the world of virtue.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Join thou on the hide these two allied stones; split apart the shoots
    (aс╣Е┼Ы├║) successfully for the sacrificer; smiting down, smite them that
    would fight her; bearing up thy progeny aloft, lift up.
Notes

The feminine participles in c, d indicate that the verse is
addressed to the wife of the sacrificer, though the comm. understands
the first half as for the priest. Aс╣Е┼Ыu he regards as applied by a
figure to the rice, as gr─Бv─Бс╣З─Бu ‘soma-pressing-stones,’ means mortar
and pestle. ‘Smite down’ and ’lift up’ are the alternate movements of
the pestle, each viewed as symbolical. Im─Бm is redundant in c as
regards both meter and sense; perhaps it has blundered in here out of
11 c. Ppp. is corrupt in c and d, but can be seen to read
uddharant─л in d. The verse and its parts are quoted in K─Бu┼Ы. 61.
18, 22, 24.

Griffith

Fix on the skin these two joined press-stones, duly rending the fibres for the sacrificer. Strike down and slay those who assail this woman, and elevating raise on high her offspring.

  1. Seize in thy hand, O hero, the two joint-acting (sakс╣Ы╠Бt) stones;
    the worshipful gods have come to thy sacrifice; three boons, whichsoever
    thou choosestтАФthose successes do I here make successful for thee.
Notes

The comm. and one or two of SPP’s authorities read sukс╣Ы╠Бt─Бu in a
(Ppp. sayuj─Б); sakс╣Ы╠Бt is not elsewhere found used as an adjective.
Ppp. further combines hasta ─Б into hast─Б in a-b, and reads
yaj├▒ey─Б and ayus in b. The comm. renders te in b as if it
were t├й. тМКThe definition of the Anukr. may perhaps mean ‘a jagat─л of
elevens (vir─Бс╕Н-jagat─л), which possesses a thirteen at the beginning,
(and which is) deficient-by-two (vir─Бс╣н).’тМЛ

Griffith

Grasp with thy hand, O man, the well-formed press-stones: the holy Gods have come unto thy worship. Three wishes of thy heart which thou electest, these happy gains for thee I here make ready.

резрез рдЗрдпрдВ рддреЗ ...{Loading}...
Whitney
Translation
  1. This [is] thy thought (? dh─лt├н) and this thy place of birth; let
    Aditi, of hero-sons, seize thee; cleanse away them that would fight her;
    confirm to her wealth with all heroes.
Notes

Said, according to K─Бu┼Ы. (61. 23), in connection with taking up the
winnowing fan (┼Ы┼лrpa). The comm. explains dh─лti as = p─Бna, taking
it from the root dh─Б ‘suck.’ One would like to derive it from dh─Б
‘put,’ as ‘place’ or something similar. Ppp. reads at the end ni
yach─Бt.

Griffith

Here thy devotion is, here is thy birthplace. Aditi, Mother of brave sons, accept thee! Wipe away those who fight against this woman with wealth and store of goodly sons endow her.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Sit ye in the wooden blower (? upa┼Ыvas├б); be ye winnowed,
    worshipful ones, from the husks. By fortune (┼Ыr─л╠Б) may we surpass all
    [our] equals; I make [our] haters to fall under foot.

Griffith

Rest in the roaring frame of wood: be parted from husk and chaff, ye Sacrificial Fibres. May we surpass in glory all our rivals. I cast beneath my feet the men who hate us.

резрей рдкрд░реЗрд╣рд┐ рдирд╛рд░рд┐ ...{Loading}...
Whitney
Translation
  1. Go away, woman; come back quickly; the stall (goс╣гс╣нh├б) of the waters
    hath ascended thee for bearing; seize then of them тМКf.тМЛ whichever shall
    be worshipful; having shared [them] out wisely, then leave the others.
Notes

The comm. explains goс╣гс╣нha by jalar─Б┼Ыi; it is rather, doubtless, the
vessel in which the water is brought, on the shoulder or head
(adhi-ruh: comm. ┼Ыirasi ─Б-ruh). тМКCf. OB. iii. 261 b.тМЛ The comm.
reads ─Бsan at end of c. Ppp. combines yaj├▒i─Б тАЩsan in c, and
in d reads vibhajya, and hvay─лta for jah─лt─Бt. SPP. reads in
b goс╣гс╣нh├│ тАШdhy, with the majority of his authorities.

Griffith

Go, Dame, and quickly come again: the waters, enclosed, have mounted thee that thou mayst bear them. Take thou of these such as are fit for service: skilfully separating. leave the others.

резрек рдПрдорд╛ рдЕрдЧреБрд░реНрдпреЛрд╖рд┐рддрдГ ...{Loading}...
Whitney
Translation
  1. These maidens (yoс╣г├нt) have come, adorning themselves; stand up,
    woman, take hold of the mighty one; well-spoused with husband,
    progeny-possessing with progeny; to thee hath come the sacrifice;
    receive thou the vessel (kumbh├б).
Notes

The comm. explains the ‘maidens’ as the ‘water-bringing women,’ but they
are evidently the waters (fem.) themselves: compare vss. 17, 27 below.
The comm. reads tava sam, two separate words, in b; тМКRoth, in his
Notes, adds that Ppp. reads tavas saс╣Б bharasvaтМЛ; the ‘mighty one’ is
the ‘vessel’ of d. Verses 13-15 are quoted in K─Бu┼Ы. (60. 25-29), but
not in natural sequence with the verses that precede and follow.

Griffith

Hither these Dames have come in radiant beauty. Arise and seize= upon thy strength, O woman. To thee hath sacrifice come: take the pitcher, blest with a good lord, children, children’s children.

резрел рдКрд░реНрдЬреЛ рднрд╛рдЧреЛ ...{Loading}...
Whitney
Translation
  1. The portion of refreshment (┼л╠Бrj) [is] set down which [is]
    yours of old; do thou, instructed by the seer, bring these waters; let
    this sacrifice be for you progress-gaining (g─Бtu-v├нd), refuge-gaining,
    progeny-gaining, formidable, cattle-gaining, hero-gaining.
Notes

‘Thou’ in b is fem., the water-bearer, doubtless, of vs. 13. The
‘yours’ of a and the ‘you’ of d refer probably to those
interested in the ceremony, though the comm. understands the former of
the waters. Ppp. reads nihatas in a, combines and reads -с╣гс╣н─Б тАЩp─Б
тАЩhar─Бi тАЩt─Бс╕е in b, puts n─Бthavid before g─Бtuvid in c, and
elides vo тАШstu in d.

Griffith

Instructed by the Rishis, bring those waters, the share of strength which was of old assigned you. Let this effectual sacrifice afford you protection, fortune, off- spring, men, and cattle.

резрем рдЕрдЧреНрдиреЗ ...{Loading}...
Whitney
Translation
  1. O Agni, the worshipful pot hath ascended thee; bright (┼Ы├║ci), very
    hot, do thou heat it with heat; let those of the seers, those of the
    gods, gathering unto their share, very hot, heat this with the seasons.
Notes

The comm. understands the epithets in b as belonging to car├║s,
which is doubtless wrong; those in c he understands of ‘Brahmans’
and ‘attendants on Indra and the other gods’; without much question, the
flames of Agni are intended. Ppp. reads in c dev─Б тАЩbhisaс╣Бhatya.
The verse plainly accompanies the setting of the vessel for boiling on
the fire: so K─Бu┼Ы. 61. 31; also 2. 7.

Griffith

Agni, on thee the sacrificial caldron hath mounted: shining,. fiercely flaming, heat it. May hottest flames, divine, sprung from the Rishis, gathering, with the Seasons, heat this portion.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Let these cleansed, purified, worshipful maidens, the waters,
    beauteous ones, creep down to the pot; they have given us abundant
    progeny, cattle; let the cooker of the rice-dish go to the world of the
    well-doers.
Notes

тМКP─Бda a is identical with vs. 27 a and vi. 122. 5 a.тМЛ The
mss. are about equally divided in c between bahul─Б╠Бm and bahul─Б╠Бn
(our I.T.K.Kp. have the latter; O. has -l─Бс╣Бn); SPP. accepts the
latter, we the former; the comm. has -l─Бn; and he reads pakv─Б for
pakt─Б in d тМКor cтМЛ. Ppp. has dadat for adus in c, and
eti for etu in d. The verse concerns the pouring in of the
water: so K─Бu┼Ы. 61. 34-5, and 2. 8.тАФтМКIf we read bahul─Б╠Бс╣Е┼Ы ca in c,
and in d pakv─Б├║danasya as a compound (against the pada-division,
which reckons pakt─Б╠Б to c, and against the double accent) and u for
etu, we get most acceptable sense and meter: lok├бm would be
construed as co├╢rdinate with pa┼Ы┼л╠Бn and pakv─Б├║danasya as co├╢rdinate
with nas (cf. xi. 8. 10 c and Speyer, Vedische Syntax, ┬з71,
end). The heroic surgery implies no worse corruptions than we have often
seen. But this is all mere suggestion.тМЛ

Griffith

Purified, bright, and holy, let these Women, these lucid waters glide into the caldron. Cattle and many children may they give us. May he who cooks. the Odana go to heaven.

Griffith

Whitney
Translation
  1. Spread thyself broad, with great greatness, thousand-backed, in the
    world of the well-done: grandfathers, fathers, progeny, descendants
    (upaj─Б╠Б): I am thy fifteen-fold cooker.
Notes

Fifteen-fold тМКcf. Skt. Gram. ┬з488тМЛ, probably, as representing so many
generations, or degrees of kindred. The verse accompanies the boiling
тМКK─Бu┼Ы. 61. 37: employed also in connection with other verses at 68. 27тМЛ,
and alludes apparently to the swelling of the mess in the process. Ppp.
combines te тАШsmi at the end. The mss. vary between pakt─Б╠Б and
paktv─Б╠Б in d (our T.K.Kp. have -t─Б╠Б) SPP. reads pakt─Б╠Б, with the
large majority of his authorities, and it is doubtless the true reading.
The comm. has again pakv─Б. тМКCorrect the Berlin ed. to pakt─Б╠Б.тМЛ

Griffith

Expand thyself abroad in all thy greatness, with thousand Prish- thas, in the world of virtue. Grandfathers, fathers, children, and descendants, fifteenth am I to thee when I have dressed it.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Thousand-backed, hundred-streamed, unexhausted, [is] the
    brahm├бn-rice-dish, god-traveled, heaven-going; them yonder I assign to
    thee; lessen (?) thou them with progeny; be gracious then to me [as]
    bringer of tribute.
Notes

K─Бu┼Ы. makes no use of this parenthetical verse of praise, prayer, and
imprecation. The comm. and two of SPP’s authorities read re┼Ыaya in
c, and the comment to Pr─Бt. iii. 94 (though reading reс╣гay─Бi тАЩn─Бn)
quotes it as an example of a palatal or lingual or dental mute
interposed between r and n, which would seem to imply recaya.*
The comm. glosses his re┼Ыaya with le┼Ыaya alp─лkuru, and, as the
expression looks as if meant for the opposite to that in vs. 21 a,
the translation has been made accordingly. тМКPpp. reads akс╣гato at end
of a.тМЛ тМКWhere the Anukr. finds a p─Бda of 13 syllables I know
not.тАФThe one of 14 must be c: does para mean simply the second
half-verse?тМЛ *тМКThat is, it implies the mute (c) rather than the
sibilant (┼Ы), the intervention of which was treated in the preceding
rule, iii. 93.тМЛ

Griffith

With thousand streams and Prishthas, undecaying, Brahmaudana is celestial, God-reaching. Those I give up to thee with all their children. Force them to tribute, but to me be gracious.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Go thou up to the sacrificial hearth; increase her with progeny;
    push [away] the demon; set her further forward; by fortune may we
    surpass all [our] equals; I make [our] haters to fall under foot.
Notes

The last half-verse is the same with vs. 12 c, d above. The whole
evidently accompanies the bringing of the cooked dish to the place of
offering: according to K─Бu┼Ы. 61. 41, its removal from the fire. Ppp.
reads enam at end of a, pratiraс╣Б dhehy enam at end of b,
pa┼Ыy─Б for ┼Ыriy─Б in c, and p─Бdayema тМКcf. vs. 12тМЛ at end of
d.

Griffith

Rise to the altar: bless this dame with offspring. Promote this woman; drive away the demons. May we surpass in glory all our rivals. I cast beneath my feet the men who hate us.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Turn thou toward her together with cattle; be opposite to her
    together with the divinities; let not curse attain thee, nor witchcraft
    (abhic─Бr├б); bear rule (vi-r─Бj) in thine own field (kс╣г├йtra), free
    from disease.
Notes

The comm. reads en─Бn in both a and b. тМКAllтМЛ pada-mss. read
anam─лv─Б╠Бс╕е in d тМКsave SPP’s J. prima manu: W’s translation and the
comm. imply -v─Б╠Б, and this SPP. has adopted as his pada-readingтМЛ.
Ppp. has in a prajay─Б sah─Бi тАЩnam, and, for c, d, a very
different (and corrupt) text: svargo lokam abhi saс╣Бvih─лnam ─Бdityo deva
parame vyoma; тМКits b is corruptтМЛ. According to K─Бu┼Ы. 61. 42, with
this verse the vessel is made to take a turn to the right. In b the
duplication of n╠Д before en─Бm is overlooked in nearly all the mss.,
and SPP. admits in his text the ungrammatical combination.

Griffith

Approach this woman here with store of cattle: together with the deities come to meet her. Let not a curse or imprecation reach thee: in thine own seat shine forth exempt from sickness.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Fashioned by righteousness (с╣Ыt├б), set by mind, this was ordained
    in the beginning the sacrificial hearth of the brahm├бn-rice-dish;
    apply, O woman, the cleansed shoulder-bearer (?); on that set the
    rice-dish of them of the gods.
Notes

SPP. reads in c aс╣Еsadr─л╠Бm, with rather the larger number of
authorities (of our mss. Bp.P.M.W.I.K.Kp.), though only -dhr─лm seems
to offer any etymology, and that an unsatisfactory one. The comm. has
aс╣Е┼Ыadhr─лm ‘portion-holder,’ which is perhaps the true reading. The
pada-text leaves the word undivided. The mss. of K─Бu┼Ы. (61. 44), it
may be noted, also vary between aс╣Еsadhr─лm and -dr─лm in quoting the
prat─лka of the second half-verse. D─Бivy─Бn─Бm would rectify the meter
of d, but no ms. reads it, though two of SPP’s, and the comm., give
dev─Бn─Бm. Ppp. reads in a manaso kite тАЩyaс╣Б, in b nihaс╣Еt─Б
for vihit─Б, in c a┼Ыadhriyaс╣Б, emended by another hand to
-ddhiyaс╣Б.

Griffith

Fashioned at first by Right, set by the spirit, this altar of Brahmau- dana was appointed. Place the pure boiler on it, woman! set thou therein the rice mess of Celestial Beings.

рдкрдгреНрдбрд┐рдд рдХреНрд╖реЗрдордХрд░рдгрджрд╛рд╕ рддреНрд░рд┐рд╡реЗрджреА - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

Whitney
Translation
  1. Aditi’s hand, this second ladle (sr├║c), which the seven seers,
    being-makers, madeтАФlet that spoon, knowing the members of the rice-dish,
    collect it upon the sacrificial hearth.
Notes

The comm. reads in a hastam and dvit─лyam, indicating that he
regards the adjective as qualifying hast─Бm rather than srucamтАФwhich
may well be the case. Ppp. тМКhas hast─Бс╣Б andтМЛ combines saptarс╣гayas.

Griffith

This second hand of Aditi, this ladle which the Seven Rishis, world-creators, fashioned. May this scoop deftly pile upon the altar, therein, the members of the rice-oblation.

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рднреВрддрдХреГрддрдГ) рдЙрдЪрд┐рдд рдХрд░реНрдо рдХрд░рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ (рд╕рдкреНрддрдЛрд╖рдпрдГ) рд╕рд╛рдд рдЛрд╖рд┐рдпреЛрдВ [рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдкрдирд╢реАрд▓ рд╡рд╛ рджрд░реНрд╢рдирд╢реАрд▓, рдЕрд░реНрдерд╛рддреН рддреНрд╡рдЪрд╛, рдиреЗрддреНрд░, рдХрд╛рди, рдЬрд┐рд╣реНрд╡рд╛, рдирд╛рдХ, рдорди рдФрд░ рдмреБрджреНрдзрд┐] рдиреЗ (рдЕрджрд┐рддреЗрдГ) рдЕрджрд┐рддрд┐ [рдЕрдЦрдгреНрдб рд╡реНрд░рддрд╡рд╛рд▓реА рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛] рдХреЗ (рдпрд╛рдореН) рдЬрд┐рд╕ (рд╣рд╕реНрддрд╛рдореН) рдЦрд┐рд▓реА рд╣реБрдИ [рдПрддрд╛рдореН] рдЗрд╕ (рджреНрд╡рд┐рддреАрдпрд╛рдореН) рджреВрд╕рд░реА [рд╢рд╛рд░реАрд░рд┐рдХ рд╕реЗ рднрд┐рдиреНрди рдорд╛рдирд╕рд┐рдХ] (рд╕реНрд░реБрдЪрдореН) рд╕реНрд░реБрдЪрд╛ [рдбреЛрдИ рдЕрд░реНрдерд╛рддреН рдЪрд┐рддреНрддрд╡реГрддреНрддрд┐] рдХреЛ (рдЕрдХреГрдгреНрд╡рдиреН) рдмрдирд╛рдпрд╛ рд╣реИ, (рдУрджрдирд╕реНрдп) рдУрджрди [рд╕реБрдЦ рдХреА рд╡рд░реНрд╖рд╛ рдХрд░рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ рдЕрдиреНрдирд░реВрдк рдкрд░рдорд╛рддреНрдорд╛] рдХреЗ (рдЧрд╛рддреНрд░рд╛рдгрд┐) рдЕрдЩреНрдЧреЛрдВ [рдЧреБрдгреЛрдВ рдХреЗ рддрддреНрддреНрд╡реЛрдВ] рдХреЛ (рд╡рд┐рджреБрд╖реА) рдЬрд╛рдирддреА рд╣реБрдИ (рд╕рд╛) рд╡рд╣ (рджрд░реНрд╡рд┐рдГ) рдХрд░рдЫреА [рдЪрд┐рддреНрддрд╡реГрддреНрддрд┐] (рд╡реЗрджреНрдпрд╛рдореН) рд╡реЗрджреА рдкрд░ [рд╣реГрджрдп рдореЗрдВ] (рдПрдирдореН) рдЗрд╕ [рдЕрдиреНрдирд░реВрдк рдкрд░рдорд╛рддреНрдорд╛] рдХреЛ (рдЕрдзрд┐) рдЕрдзрд┐рдХ-рдЕрдзрд┐рдХ (рдЪрд┐рдиреЛрддреБ) рдПрдХрддреНрд░ рдХрд░реЗ реереирекрее

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд┐рдпреЛрдВ рджреНрд╡рд╛рд░рд╛ рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпреЛрдВ рдХреЗ рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рди рд╕реЗ рдмрд╛рд╣рд┐рд░реА рдФрд░ рднреАрддрд░реА рджреЛ рд╡реГрддреНрддрд┐рдпрд╛рдБ рдЙрддреНрдкрдиреНрди рд╣реЛрддреА рд╣реИрдВред рдмрд╛рд╣рд┐рд░реА рд╡реГрддреНрддрд┐ рднреАрддрд░реА рд╡реГрддреНрддрд┐ рдХреЗ рдЖрдзреАрди рд╣реИред рдпреЛрдЧреА рдХреЛ рдЙрдЪрд┐рдд рд╣реИ рдХрд┐ рднреАрддрд░реА рд╡реГрддреНрддрд┐рдпреЛрдВ рдХреЛ рдкрд░рдорд╛рддреНрдорд╛ рдХреЗ рдЧреБрдгреЛрдВ рдореЗрдВ рд▓рдЧрд╛рдХрд░ рдЙрд╕ рдЬрдЧрджреАрд╢реНрд╡рд░ рдХреЛ рдЕрдкрдиреЗ рд╣реГрджрдп рдореЗрдВ рдмреИрдард╛рд╡реЗ, рдЬреИрд╕реЗ рд╡реЗрджреА рдкрд░ рдЪрдврд╝реА рдмрдЯрд▓реЛрд╣реА рдХреЗ рдШреГрдд рдЖрджрд┐ рдХреЛ рдХрд░рдЫреА рд╕реЗ рд╕рдВрднрд╛рд▓-рд╕рдВрднрд╛рд▓ рдХрд░ рдЙрдкрдХрд╛рд░реА рдмрдирд╛рддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ реереирекрее

Whitney
Translation
  1. Let them of the gods sit by thee, a cooked (┼Ыс╣Ыt├б) oblation; having
    crept out of the fire, sit thou forward again to them; purified by soma,
    sit thou in the belly of the worshipers (brahm├бn); let not them of the
    seers, partakers (pr─Б┼Ыitс╣Ы╠Б) of thee, suffer harm.

of SPP’s authoritiesтМЛ reads dev─Бs at end of a, and treats te in

‘four ─Бrс╣гeyas, who know the bhс╣Ыgvan╠Дgiras’ by the offering.

Griffith

Let the dressed offering and divine Ones serve thee: creep from. the fire again, own these as masters. Made pure with Soma rest within the Brahmans: let not thine eaters, Rishis’ sons, be injured.

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - [рд╣реЗ рдУрджрди] (рджреИрд╡рд╛рдГ) рдЙрддреНрддрдо рдЧреБрдгрд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ рдкреБрд░реБрд╖ (рд╢реГрддрдореН) рдкрд░рд┐рдкрдХреНрд╡, (рд╣рд╡реНрдпрдореН) рдЧреНрд░рд╣рдг рдХрд░рдиреЗ рдпреЛрдЧреНрдп (рддреНрд╡рд╛ рдЙрдк) рддреЗрд░реЗ рд╕рдореАрдк (рд╕реАрджрдиреНрддреБ) рдмреИрдареЗрдВ, (рдЕрдЧреНрдиреЗрдГ) рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐ рд╕реЗ (рдирд┐рдГрд╕реГрдкреНрдп) рдирд┐рдХрд▓рдХрд░ (рдкреБрдирдГ) рдЕрд╡рд╢реНрдп (рдПрдирд╛рдореН) рдЗрди [рдкреБрд░реБрд╖реЛрдВ] рдХреЛ (рдкреНрд░рд╕реАрдж) рдкреНрд░рд╕рдиреНрди рдХрд░ред (рд╕реЛрдореЗрди) рдЕрдореГрдд рд░рд╕ рд╕реЗ (рдкреВрддрдГ) рд╢реЛрдзрд╛ рд╣реБрдЖ рддреВ (рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдордгрд╛рдореН) рдмреНрд░рд╛рд╣реНрдордгреЛрдВ [рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдордЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирд┐рдпреЛрдВ] рдХреЗ (рдЬрдард░реЗ) рдкреЗрдЯ рдореЗрдВ (рд╕реАрдж) рдмреИрда, (рддреЗ) рддреЗрд░реЗ (рдкреНрд░рд╛рд╢рд┐рддрд╛рд░рдГ) рднреЛрдЧ рдХрд░рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ (рдЖрд░реНрд╖реЗрдпрд╛рдГ) рдЛрд╖рд┐рдпреЛрдВ рдореЗрдВ рд╡рд┐рдЦреНрдпрд╛рдд рдкреБрд░реБрд╖ (рдорд╛ рд░рд┐рд╖рдиреН) рди рджреБрдГрдЦреА рд╣реЛрд╡реЗрдВ реереирелрее

Whitney
Translation
  1. O king Soma, strew harmony for them, for whatsoever good Brahmans
    shall sit by thee; with good call, I call loudly to the
    brahm├бn-rice-dish the seers, them of the seers, born from penance
    (t├бpas).
Notes

In a-b, for -bhyaс╕е s├║bс╣Ы─Бhmaс╣З─Бs, Ppp. reads -bhyo br─Бhm-
тМКintending perhaps ├бbr─Бhmaс╣З─Бs? cf. vs. 32тМЛ; in c it has с╣Ыс╣г─лс╣З─Бm
с╣Ыс╣гayas tap-, and j─Бt─Б (so also the comm.) for -t─Бn; тМКand begins
d with br─Бhm─БudaneтМЛ. The comm. understands suhav─Б in d as
fem., and makes the sacrificer’s wife the speaker. The verse is not
quoted in K─Бu┼Ы.; тМКbut Ke┼Ыava cites it just before vs. 25 in 63. 3тМЛ.

Griffith

Give understanding unto these, King Soma! all the good Brah mans who attend and serve thee. Oft, in Brahmaudana, and well I call on: Rishis, their sons, and those who sprang from Fervour.

    field, this my desire-milker; this riches I deposit in the Brahmans; I
    make a road to the Fathers that is heaven-going.

d. The verse is quoted by K─Бu┼Ы. at 62. 22 and 68. 27; and at 63. 5

something (ity apakarс╣гati: it is not clear what; тМКthe comm. thinks the
rice-dish and reads upa- for apa-тМЛ).

Griffith

Here is my gold, a light immortal: ripened grain from the field this Cow of Plenty give me! This wealth I place among the Brahmans, making a path that leads to heaven among the Fathers.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Strew thou the husks in the fire, in J─Бtavedas; wipe off far away
    the chaff (? kamb┼л╠Бk─Бn); this we have heard to be the share of the
    house-king; also we know the portion (bh─Бgadh├йya) of Perdition
    (n├нrс╣Ыti).
Notes

Ppp. reads upa mс╣Ыс╕Нhvayet─Бm for apa mс╣Ыс╕Нс╕Нhi d┼лram in b. The comm.
explains kamb┼лk─Бn as = phal─лkaraс╣З─Бn, and follows K─Бu┼Ы. (63. 7) in
regarding the ‘wiping away’ as done with the foot.

Griffith

Lay thou the chaff in Agni Jatavedas: remove the husks and drive them to a distance. That, we have heard, that is the House-Lord’s portion: we know the share allotted to Destruction.

рдЕреТрдЧреНрдиреМред рддреБрд╖рд╛реСрдиреНред рдЖред рд╡реТрдкреТред рдЬрд╛реТрддрд╜рд╡реЗреСрджрд╕рд┐ред рдкреТрд░рдГред рдХреТрдореНрдмреВрдХрд╛реСрдиреНред рдЕрдкреСред рдореГреТрдбреНрдврд┐реТред рджреВреТрд░рдореНред рдПреТрддрдореНред рд╢реБреТрд╢реНрд░реБреТрдореТред рдЧреГреТрд╣реТрд╜рд░рд╛реТрдЬрд╕реНрдпреСред рднрд╛реТрдЧрдореНред рдЕрдереЛреТ рдЗрддрд┐реСред рд╡рд┐реТрджреНрдореТред рдирд┐рдГрд╜рдЛреСрддреЗрдГред рднрд╛реТрдЧреТрд╜рдзреЗрдпреСрдореНред рез.реирепред

рейреж рд╢реНрд░рд╛рдореНрдпрддрдГ рдкрдЪрддреЛ ...{Loading}...
Whitney
Translation
  1. Know thou the toiling, cooking, soma-pressing one; make him to
    ascend the heaven-going road, by which he may ascend, arriving at the
    vigor that is beyond, to the highest firmament, to the furthest vault
    (vy├▓mati).
Notes

‘Know,’ i.e. take note or be mindful of. The comm. takes the three
participles in a as accus. pl. instead of gen. sing.; тМКand reads
accordingly en─Бn at end of bтМЛ. Ppp. has, for b, svargaс╣Б lokam
adhi rohaye тАЩnam, and omits d. The quotation in K─Бu┼Ы. 63. 20 casts
no light on the verse.

Griffith

Mark him who toils and cooks and pours oblation: make this man climb the path that leads to heaven, That he may mount and reach life that is highest, ascending to the loftiest vault above us.

рдкрджрдкрд╛рдардГ

рд╢реНрд░рд╛рдореНрдпреСрддрдГред рдкрдЪреСрддрдГред рд╡рд┐реТрдзреНрджрд┐реТред рд╕реБреТрдиреНрд╡реТрддрдГред рдкрдиреНрдерд╛реСрдореНред рд╕реНрд╡рдГреТрд╜рдЧрдореНред рдЕрдзрд┐реСред рд░реЛреТрд╣реТрдпреТред рдПреТрдиреТрдореНред рдпреЗрдиреСред рд░реЛрд╣рд╛реСрддреНред рдкрд░реСрдореНред рдЖреТрд╜рдкрджреНрдпреСред рдпрддреНред рд╡рдпрдГреСред рдЙреТрддреНрд╜рддреТрдордореНред рдирд╛рдХреСрдореНред рдкреТрд░реТрдордореНред рд╡рд┐рд╜рдУреСрдоред рез.рейрежред

Whitney
Translation
  1. Wipe off, O serving priest (adhvary├║), this face of the bearing
    one (? babhr├н); make thou, understanding it, room for the sacrificial
    butter; wipe off with ghee along all [its] members; I make a road to
    the Fathers that is heaven-going.
Notes

The real sense of the epithet babhri applied to the odana or
rice-dish is obscure; the comm. explains it here with bharaс╣Зa┼Ы─лlasya
poс╣гakasya pakvasy─Б odanasya, ‘supporting’ or ’nourishing.’ The comm.
appears to read vidv─Бn instead of pravidv─Бn in b; Ppp. has
praj─Бnan. Ppp. has yat for yas in d. According to K─Бu┼Ы. 62.
15, the verse accompanies the making of an ─Бp─Бna (? the mss. vary as
to the word) above (upari); which the comm. explains by odanasyo
тАЩpari gartaс╣Б kury─Бt, glossing lokam in b with sth─Бnaс╣Б
gartar┼лpam; what is meant is obscure.

Griffith

Adhvaryu, cleanse that face of the Supporter. Make room, well knowing, for the molten butter. Purify duly all the limbs with fatness. I make a path to heaven amid the Fathers.

Whitney
Translation
  1. O bearing one, [as] a demon, strew discord for them, for
    whatsoever non-Brahmans shall sit by thee; rich in ground (? pur─лс╣г├нn),
    spreading themselves forward, let not them of the seers, partakers of
    thee, suffer harm.
Notes

With the first half-verse compare vs. 26 a, b, above; the last p─Бda
is the same with 25 d. The construction of r├бkс╣гas in a is
doubtful; it might be vocative; the comm. combines it into a compound
with samadam; and he treats te, as before, as if it were t├й. Ppp.
reads at beginning of b, as our text in vs. 26, subr─Бhmaс╣З─Бs. The
verse is not quoted in K─Бu┼Ы.

Griffith

Supporter, send to those men fiends and battle, to all non-Brah- mans who attend and serve thee. Famous and foremost, with their great possessions, let not these here, the Rishis sons, be injured.

Whitney
Translation
  1. I set thee down, O rice-dish, among them of the seers; for them that
    are not of the seers there is no portion here; let Agni my guardian, and
    all the Maruts, let all the gods defend the cooked [offering].
Notes

‘Is no portion for,’ lit’ly ‘is not also (api) ofтАФa common form of
expression in the Br─Бhmaс╣Зas. Ppp. reads rakс╣гanti in d. The verse
is quoted with vs. 25 c in K─Бu┼Ы. 65. 12.

Griffith

I set thee, Odana, with Rishis’ children: naught here belongs to men not sprung from Rishis. Let Agni my protector, all the Maruts, the Visve Devas guard the cooked oblation.

Whitney
Translation
  1. The offering, yielding milk (duh), constantly full (pr├бp─лna), a
    male (p├║m─Бс╣Еs) milch-cow, seat of wealth, immortality through
    offspring, and a long life-timeтАФand may we sit by thee with abundance
    (pl.) of wealth.
Notes

The construction of the third p─Бda is very indeterminate; the words may
be either nominative or accusative; they express in some way what the
offering is to procure. To illustrate praj─Бmс╣Ыtatvam, the comm. quotes,
quite appositely, TB. i. 5. 5тБ╢ and RV. v. 4. 10, ‘by progeny, O Agni,
may I obtain immortality.’ Prap─лnam he explains as =
pravс╣Ыddhodhaskam, which is doubtless its true meaning. Ppp. reads in
d poс╣гam for poс╣г─Бis. Neither this nor the following verse, nor
vs. 37, is quoted in K─Бu┼Ы. тМКCf. Henry’s version, p. 102; and, for the
awkward ca, his note, p. 139.тМЛ

Griffith

May we adore thee, Sacrifice that yieldeth an everlasting son, cow, home of treasures, Together with increasing store of riches, long life and immor- tality of children.

Translation
  1. Thou art a heaven-going bull; go to the seers, to them of the seers;
    sit in the world of the well-doing; there is there preparation
    (saс╣Бskс╣Ыt├б) for us both.

s─лdata t├бn naс╕е saс╣Бskс╣Ыt├бm; and VS. iv. 34 has the last p─Бda, reading
t├бn for t├бtra. The pada-texts do not divide saс╣Бskс╣Ыtam; the case

Griffith

Thou art a Bull that mounts to heaven: to Rishis and their off- spring go. Rest in the world of pious men: there is the place prepared for us.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Gather thou together unto, go thou together forth after; O Agni,
    make ready (kalpay-) the roads traveled by the gods; by them,
    well-made, may we go after the offering, that stands upon the
    seven-rayed firmament.

All the mss. тМКsave one or two of SPP’sтМЛ leave agne unaccented, as if
it belonged to a, and Bp. puts the double division-mark after it
accordingly; SPP. reads with the тМКmajority of hisтМЛ mss.; we have made
the necessary emendation to ├бgne. Ppp. reads at the beginning
sam─Бtanuс╣гva; for c it has yebhis sukс╣Ыt─Бir anu praj├▒eс╣гс╣нhaс╣Еs sa
yaj├▒e. The comm. regards a as addressed to the rice-dish, which is
to ‘gather up ’ all its members. The verse is quoted in K─Бu┼Ы. 63. 9, but
not in a way to cast any light upon it. TS. iv. 7. 13тБ┤ and MS. ii. 12. 4
are to be compared with the first half-verse, but they vary much from it
and from one another.

Griffith

Level the ways: go thitherward, O Agni. Make ready thou the Godward-leading pathways. By these our pious actions may we follow sacrifice dwelling in the seven-rayed heaven.

Translation
  1. With what light the gods went up to the sky, having cooked the
    brahm├бn-rice-dish, to the world of the well-done, with that may we go
    to the world of the well-done, ascending the heaven, unto the highest
    firmament.

Griffith

May we invested with that light go upward, ascending to the sky’s most lofty summit. Wherewith the Gods, what time they had made ready Brahmaudana, mounted to the world of virtue.

рдкрдгреНрдбрд┐рдд рдХреНрд╖реЗрдордХрд░рдгрджрд╛рд╕ рддреНрд░рд┐рд╡реЗрджреА - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЬрд┐рд╕ рд╡реИрджрд┐рдХ рдЬреНрдпреЛрддрд┐ рджреНрд╡рд╛рд░рд╛ рд╡рд┐рдЬрдпреА рдорд╣рд╛рддреНрдорд╛ рд▓реЛрдЧреЛрдВ рдиреЗ рдЪрд▓рдХрд░ рдкрд░рдорд╛рддреНрдорд╛ рдХреЛ рдкрд╛рдпрд╛ рд╣реИ, рдЙрд╕реА рд╡реИрджрд┐рдХ рдЬреНрдпреЛрддрд┐ рджреНрд╡рд╛рд░рд╛ рдкрд░рдорд╛рддреНрдорд╛ рдХреЛ рджреЗрдЦрддреЗ рд╣реБрдП рд╣рдо рд╕рдм рдкреБрдгреНрдпрд╛рддреНрдорд╛рдУрдВ рдХреЗ рдмреАрдЪ рд╕реБрдЦ рдкрд╛рд╡реЗрдВ реерейренреердЗрд╕ рдордиреНрддреНрд░ рдХрд╛ рдЙрддреНрддрд░рд╛рд░реНрдз рдЖ рдЪреБрдХрд╛ рд╣реИ-рдЕреж рекредрезрекредрем рее

рдкрдгреНрдбрд┐рдд рдХреНрд╖реЗрдордХрд░рдгрджрд╛рд╕ рддреНрд░рд┐рд╡реЗрджреА - рдкрд╛рджрдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдиреА

рдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдгреА: рейрентИТ(рдпреЗрди) (рджреЗрд╡рд╛рдГ) рд╡рд┐рдЬрд┐рдЧреАрд╖рд╡рдГ (рдЬреНрдпреЛрддрд┐рд╖рд╛) рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢реЗрди (рджреНрдпрд╛рдореН) рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢рдорд╛рдирдореН (рдЙрджрд╛рдпрдиреН) рдЗрдгреН рдЧрддреМ-рд▓рдЩреНред рдЙрджрдЧрдЪреНрдЫрдиреН (рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдореМрджрдирдореН) рдореж резред рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдордгреЛ рд╡реЗрджрдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирд╕реНрдпрд╛рдиреНрдирд╕реНрдп рдзрдирд╕реНрдп рд╡рд╛ рд╕реЗрдЪрдХрдВ рд╡рд░реНрд╖рдХрдВ рдкрд░рдорд╛рддреНрдорд╛рдирдореН (рдкрдХреНрддреНрд╡рд╛) рджреГрдврдВ рдХреГрддреНрд╡рд╛ (рд╕реБрдХреГрддрд╕реНрдп) рд╕реБрдХрд░реНрдордгрдГ (рд▓реЛрдХрдореН) рд╕рдорд╛рдЬрдореН (рдЧреЗрд╖реНрдо) рдЧреЗрд╖реГ рдЕрдиреНрд╡рд┐рдЪреНрдЫрд╛рдпрд╛рдореН-рд▓реЛрдЯреНред рдЧреЗрд╖рд╛рдорд╣реИред рдЕрдиреНрд╡реЗрд╖рдгреЗрди рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдирд╡рд╛рдордГред рдЕрдиреНрдпрддреН рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╡рддреН-рдЕреж рекредрезрекредрем рее
